pipe</a></li><li><a class="block text-sm border-l-2 pl-4 -ml-px py-1 mb-1 sm:py-0 transition-all border-transparent hover:border-v-border-active hover:font-semibold hover:underline hover:text-black" building</div></div></a><a class="text-button text-center py-1" href="https://ui.tinybird.co/login">Sign In</a></div></div></div></nav></aside><main class="w-full grow pt-6 pb-6 md:pt-8 sm:pb-8 md:max-w-[calc(100%_-var(--sidebar-width))]" data-pagefind-body=""><div class="hidden sm:block relative max-w-7xl mx-auto px-5 md:px-6 "><nav aria-label="Breadcrumb" class="py-4 max-w-4xl md:px-4 mb-2"><ol class="flex items-center text-sm"><li><a class="hover:font-semibold hover:underline hover:text-black" href="/docs/forward/get-started/quickstarts">Home</a></li><li class="flex items-center"><span class="mx-2 text-v-text-3">/</span><a class="hover:font-semibold hover:underline hover:text-black" href="/docs/forward/work-with-data">Work with data</a></li><li class="flex items-center"><span class="mx-2 text-v-text-3">/</span><a class="hover:font-semibold hover:underline hover:text-black" href="/docs/forward/work-with-data/publish-data">Publish data</a></li><li class="flex items-center"><span class="mx-2 text-v-text-3">/</span><span class="font-semibold">Endpoints</span></li></ol></nav></div><div class="relative max-w-7xl mx-auto px-5 md:px-6 xl:grid xl:grid-cols-[1fr_280px]"><div class="max-w-4xl text-body md:px-4 md:pb-20 relative" role="main"><article><div class="flex flex-col sm:flex-row sm:items-center justify-between gap-4 mb-6"><h1 id="endpoints" class="t-h3" data-pagefind-weight="20.0"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 16 17" class="inline"><path fill="#25283D" d="M7 4.063a.667.667 0 1 0 0 1.333.667.667 0 0 0 0-1.333m-2 0a.667.667 0 1 0 0 1.333.667.667 0 0 0 0-1.333m4 0a.667.667 0 1 0 0 1.333.667.667 0 0 0 0-1.333m4-2.667H3.667a2 2 0 0 0-2 2v9.333a2 2 0 0 0 2 2H13a2 2 0 0 0 2-2V3.396a2 2 0 0 0-2-2m.667 11.333a.667.667 0 0 1-.667.667H3.667A.667.667 0 0 1 3 12.729V8.063h10.667zm0-6H3V3.396a.667.667 0 0 1 .667-.667H13a.667.667 0 0 1 .667.667z"></path></svg> Endpoints<a class="headerlink" href="#endpoints" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h1><div class="flex-shrink-0 w-auto"><div class="relative inline-block w-auto" data-pagefind-ignore="true"><div class="flex rounded-md overflow-hidden border border-v-border-02 hover:border-v-border-03 transition-colors"><button class="flex items-center gap-1.5 px-3 py-1.5 text-sm transition-colors min-w-[106px] text-v-text-01"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" stroke-width="2" viewBox="0 0 24 24" class="w-4 h-4 dark:invert-[0.85] dark:brightness-[0.9]"><path d="M14 2H6a2 2 0 0 0-2 2v16a2 2 0 0 0 2 2h12a2 2 0 0 0 2-2V8z"></path><path d="M14 2v6h6M16 13H8M16 17H8M10 9H8"></path></svg><span>Copy as MD</span></button><button class="flex items-center justify-center px-2 py-1.5 text-sm text-v-text-01 border-l border-v-border-02 min-w-[32px]" aria-haspopup="true" aria-expanded="false"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" fill="none" class="w-3 h-3 dark:invert-[0.85] dark:brightness-[0.9]" style="margin-top:-4px;margin-left:-4px"><path fill="currentColor" d="M8.1 11.41 4 6.995 4.745 6 8.1 9.795 11.454 6l.746.994z"></path></svg></button></div></div></div></div><p>Endpoints are a type of pipe that you can call from other applications. For example, you can ingest your data, build SQL logic inside a pipe, and then publish the result of your query as a REST API endpoint.</p><h2 id="create-an-endpoint" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">Create an endpoint<a class="headerlink" href="#create-an-endpoint" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><p>Endpoints are defined in a .pipe file using the <code>TYPE ENDPOINT</code> directive. See <a href="/docs/forward/dev-reference/datafiles/pipe-files#endpoint-pipes">Endpoint pipes</a>.</p><p>You can list your endpoints and their URLs and tokens using the <code>tb endpoint</code> command. See <a href="/docs/forward/dev-reference/commands/tb-endpoint">tb endpoint</a>.</p><h2 id="query-parameters" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">Query parameters<a class="headerlink" href="#query-parameters" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><p>Query parameters are great for any value of the query that you might want control dynamically from your applications. For example, you can get your endpoint to answer different questions by passing a different value as query parameter.</p><p>Use dynamic parameters means to do things like:</p><ul><li>Filtering as part of a <code>WHERE</code> clause.</li><li>Changing the number of results as part of a <code>LIMIT</code> clause.</li><li>Sorting order as part of an <code>ORDER BY</code> clause.</li><li>Selecting specific columns for <code>ORDER BY</code> or <code>GROUP BY</code> clauses.</li></ul><h3 id="define-dynamic-parameters" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Define dynamic parameters<a class="headerlink" href="#define-dynamic-parameters" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>To make a query dynamic, start the query with a <code>%</code> character. That signals the engine that it needs to parse potential parameters.</p><p>After you have created a dynamic query, you can define parameters by using the following pattern <code>{{&lt;data_type&gt;(&lt;name_of_parameter&gt;[,&lt;default_value&gt;, description=&lt;&quot;This is a description&quot;&gt;, required=&lt;True|False&gt;])}}</code>. For example:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="Simple select clause using dynamic parameters">Simple select clause using dynamic parameters</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">%
SELECT * FROM TR LIMIT {{Int32(lim, 10, description=&quot;Limit the number of rows in the response&quot;, required=False)}}
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>The previous query returns 10 results by default, or however many are specified on the <code>lim</code> parameter when requesting data from that API endpoint.</p><div class="my-4 flex items-start gap-2 py-3 px-4 rounded border border-v-border bg-v-callout-caution text-[#856100]"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 16 16" class="inline shrink-0 mt-px h-5"><path fill="currentColor" d="M8.333 10.216a.666.666 0 1 0 0 1.332.666.666 0 0 0 0-1.332m7.114.98L10.08 1.862a2 2 0 0 0-3.493 0l-5.334 9.334a2 2 0 0 0 1.707 3.02h10.747a2 2 0 0 0 1.74-3.02m-1.154 1.333a.67.67 0 0 1-.586.34H2.96a.67.67 0 0 1-.587-.34.67.67 0 0 1 0-.667L7.707 2.53a.667.667 0 0 1 1.186 0l5.367 9.333a.67.67 0 0 1 .033.68zm-5.96-7.647a.667.667 0 0 0-.666.667v2.667a.667.667 0 1 0 1.333 0V5.549a.667.667 0 0 0-.667-.667"></path></svg><div class="text-v-text"><p>Boolean data type does not support the <code>description</code> or <code>required</code> arguments.</p></div></div><h3 id="call-an-endpoint-with-dynamic-parameters" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Call an endpoint with dynamic parameters<a class="headerlink" href="#call-an-endpoint-with-dynamic-parameters" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>When using an endpoint that uses parameters, pass in the desired parameters.</p><p>Using the previous example where <code>lim</code> sets the amount of maximum rows you want to get, the request would look like this:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="Using an endpoint containing dynamic parameters">Using an endpoint containing dynamic parameters</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">curl -d https://api.europe-west2.gcp.tinybird.co/v0/pipes/tr_pipe?lim=20&amp;token=&lt;your_token&gt;
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h3 id="available-data-types-for-dynamic-parameters" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Available data types for dynamic parameters<a class="headerlink" href="#available-data-types-for-dynamic-parameters" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>You can use the following data types for dynamic parameters:</p><ul><li><code>Boolean</code>: Accepts <code>True</code> and <code>False</code> as values, as well as strings like <code>&#x27;TRUE&#x27;</code>, <code>&#x27;FALSE&#x27;</code>, <code>&#x27;true&#x27;</code>, <code>&#x27;false&#x27;</code>, <code>&#x27;1&#x27;</code>, or <code>&#x27;0&#x27;</code>, or the integers <code>1</code> and <code>0</code>.</li><li><code>String</code>: For any string values.</li><li><code>DateTime64</code>, <code>DateTime</code> and <code>Date</code>: Accepts values like <code>YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS.MMM</code>, <code>YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS</code> and <code>YYYYMMDD</code> respectively.</li><li><code>Float32</code> and <code>Float64</code>: Accepts floating point numbers of either 32 or 64 bit precision.</li><li><code>Int</code> or <code>Integer</code>: Accepts integer numbers of any precision.</li><li><code>Int8</code>, <code>Int16</code>, <code>Int32</code>, <code>Int64</code>, <code>Int128</code>, <code>Int256</code> and <code>UInt8</code>, <code>UInt16</code>, <code>UInt32</code>, <code>UInt64</code>, <code>UInt128</code>, <code>UInt256</code>: Accepts signed or unsigned integer numbers of the specified precision.</li></ul><h3 id="use-column-parameters" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Use column parameters<a class="headerlink" href="#use-column-parameters" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>You can use <code>column</code> to pass along column names of a defined type as parameters, like:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="Using column dynamic parameters">Using column dynamic parameters</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">%
SELECT * FROM TR 
ORDER BY {{column(order_by, &#x27;timestamp&#x27;)}}
LIMIT {{Int32(lim, 10)}}
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>Always define the <code>column</code> function&#x27;s second argument, the one for the default value. The alternative for not defining the argument is to validate that the first argument is defined, but this only has an effect on the execution of the endpoint. A placeholder is used in the development of the pipes.</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="Validate the column parameter when not defining a default value">Validate the column parameter when not defining a default value</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">%
SELECT * FROM TR
{% if defined(order_by) %}
ORDER BY {{column(order_by)}}
{% end %}
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h3 id="pass-arrays" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Pass arrays<a class="headerlink" href="#pass-arrays" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>You can pass along a list of values with the <code>Array</code> function for parameters, like so:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="Passing arrays as dynamic parameters">Passing arrays as dynamic parameters</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">%
SELECT * FROM TR WHERE 
access_type IN {{Array(access_numbers, &#x27;Int32&#x27;, default=&#x27;101,102,110&#x27;)}}
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h3 id="send-stringified-json-as-parameter" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Send stringified JSON as parameter<a class="headerlink" href="#send-stringified-json-as-parameter" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>Consider the following stringified JSON:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">&quot;filters&quot;: [
    {
        &quot;operand&quot;: &quot;date&quot;,
        &quot;operator&quot;: &quot;equals&quot;,
        &quot;value&quot;: &quot;2018-01-02&quot;
    },
    {
        &quot;operand&quot;: &quot;high&quot;,
        &quot;operator&quot;: &quot;greater_than&quot;,
        &quot;value&quot;: &quot;100&quot;
    },
    {
        &quot;operand&quot;: &quot;symbol&quot;,
        &quot;operator&quot;: &quot;in_list&quot;,
        &quot;value&quot;: &quot;AAPL,AMZN&quot;
    }
]
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>You can use the <code>JSON()</code> function to use <code>filters</code> as a query parameter. The following example shows to use the <code>filters</code> field from the JSON snippet with the stock_prices_1m sample dataset.</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">%
SELECT symbol, date, high
FROM stock_prices_1m
WHERE
    1
    {% if defined(filters) %}
        {% for item in JSON(filters, &#x27;[]&#x27;) %}
            {% if item.get(&#x27;operator&#x27;, &#x27;&#x27;) == &#x27;equals&#x27; %}
                AND {{ column(item.get(&#x27;operand&#x27;, &#x27;&#x27;)) }} == {{ item.get(&#x27;value&#x27;, &#x27;&#x27;) }}
            {% elif item.get(&#x27;operator&#x27;) == &#x27;greater_than&#x27; %}
                AND {{ column(item.get(&#x27;operand&#x27;, &#x27;&#x27;)) }} &gt; {{ item.get(&#x27;value&#x27;, &#x27;&#x27;) }}
            {% elif item.get(&#x27;operator&#x27;) == &#x27;in_list&#x27; %}
                AND {{ column(item.get(&#x27;operand&#x27;, &#x27;&#x27;)) }} IN splitByChar(&#x27;,&#x27;,{{ item.get(&#x27;value&#x27;, &#x27;&#x27;) }})
            {% end %}
        {% end %}
    {% end %}
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>When accessing the fields in a JSON object, use the following syntax:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">item.get(&#x27;Field&#x27;, &#x27;Default value to avoid SQL errors&#x27;).
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h2 id="pagination" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">Pagination<a class="headerlink" href="#pagination" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><p>You can paginate results by adding <code>LIMIT</code> and <code>OFFSET</code> clauses to your query. You can parameterize the values of these clauses, allowing you to pass pagination values as query parameters to your endpoint.</p><p>Use the <code>LIMIT</code> clause to select only the first <code>n</code> rows of a query result. Use the <code>OFFSET</code> clause to skip <code>n</code> rows from the beginning of a query result. Together, you can dynamically chunk the results of a query up into pages.</p><p>For example, the following query introduces two dynamic parameters <code>page_size</code> and <code>page</code> which lets you control the pagination of a query result using query parameters on the URL of an endpoint.</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="Paging results using dynamic parameters">Paging results using dynamic parameters</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">%
SELECT * FROM TR
LIMIT {{Int32(page_size, 100)}}
OFFSET {{Int32(page, 0) * Int32(page_size, 100)}}
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>You can also use pages to perform calculations such as <code>count()</code>. The following example counts the total number of pages:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="Operation on a paginated endpoint">Operation on a paginated endpoint</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">%
SELECT count() as total_rows, ceil(total_rows/{{Int32(page_size, 100)}}) pages FROM endpoint_to_paginate
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>The addition of a <code>LIMIT</code> clause to a query also adds the <code>rows_before_limit_at_least</code> field to the response metadata. <code>rows_before_limit_at_least</code> is the lower bound on the number of rows returned by the query after transformations but before the limit was applied, and can be useful for response handling calculations.</p><p><strong>Example:</strong></p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">SELECT * FROM users WHERE active = true LIMIT 10
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>Response might include:</p><ul><li><code>rows</code>: 10 (actual rows returned)</li><li><code>rows_before_limit_at_least</code>: 1,000 (at least this many active users exist)</li></ul><p><strong>Why &quot;at least&quot;?</strong> ClickHouse can stop counting once it knows the answer exceeds the <code>LIMIT</code> value. This makes it a lower bound, not an exact count.</p><p><strong>Useful for:</strong></p><ul><li>Pagination logic (&quot;showing 10 of at least 1,247 results&quot;)</li><li>Determining if more results exist without running a separate <code>COUNT()</code> query</li></ul><p>This metadata is returned automatically with any <code>LIMIT</code> query, saving you from running an additional <code>COUNT(*)</code> query to check if more results are available.</p><div class="my-4 flex items-start gap-2 py-3 px-4 rounded border border-v-border bg-v-callout-tip text-brand-dark"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 16 16" class="inline shrink-0 mt-px h-5"><path fill="currentColor" d="M11.393 1.88A5.33 5.33 0 0 0 6.94.773a5.33 5.33 0 0 0-4.18 4.214A5.38 5.38 0 0 0 3.907 9.42c.469.53.738 1.206.76 1.913v2a2 2 0 0 0 2 2h2.666a2 2 0 0 0 2-2V11.46c.023-.78.31-1.53.814-2.127a5.334 5.334 0 0 0-.754-7.466zM10 13.333a.667.667 0 0 1-.667.667H6.667A.667.667 0 0 1 6 13.333v-.666h4zm1.113-4.826A4.75 4.75 0 0 0 10 11.333H8.667v-2a.667.667 0 0 0-1.334 0v2H6A4.33 4.33 0 0 0 4.933 8.56a4 4 0 0 1 4.02-6.447A4 4 0 0 1 12 6c.005.913-.309 1.8-.887 2.507"></path></svg><div class="text-v-text"><p>To get consistent pagination results, add an <code>ORDER BY</code> clause to your paginated queries.</p></div></div><h2 id="advanced-templating" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">Advanced templating<a class="headerlink" href="#advanced-templating" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><p>To build more complex queries, use flow control operators like <code>if</code>, <code>else</code> and <code>elif</code> in combination with the <code>defined()</code> function, which helps you to check if a parameter whether a parameter has been received and act accordingly.</p><p>Tinybird&#x27;s templating system is based on the <a href="https://github.com/tornadoweb/tornado" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" class="inline-flex items-center">Tornado Python framework</a>, and uses Python syntax. You must enclose control statements in curly brackets with percentages <code>{%..%}</code> as in the following example:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="Advanced templating using dynamic parameters">Advanced templating using dynamic parameters</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">%
SELECT
  toDate(start_datetime) as day,
  countIf(status_code &lt; 400) requests,
  countIf(status_code &gt;= 400) errors,
  avg(duration) avg_duration
FROM
  log_events
WHERE
  endsWith(user_email, {{String(email, &#x27;gmail.com&#x27;)}}) AND 
  start_datetime &gt;= {{DateTime(start_date, &#x27;2019-09-20 00:00:00&#x27;)}} AND
  start_datetime &lt;= {{DateTime(end_date, &#x27;2019-10-10 00:00:00&#x27;)}}
  {% if method != &#x27;All&#x27; %} AND method = {{String(method,&#x27;POST&#x27;)}} {% end %}
GROUP BY
  day
ORDER BY
  day DESC
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h3 id="validate-presence-of-a-parameter" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Validate presence of a parameter<a class="headerlink" href="#validate-presence-of-a-parameter" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>To validate if a parameter is present in the query, use the <code>defined()</code> function. For example:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="Validate if a param is in the query">Validate if a param is in the query</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">%
select * from table
{% if defined(my_filter) %}
where attr &gt; {{Int32(my_filter)}}
{% end %}
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>When you call the endpoint with <code>/v0/pipes/:PIPE.json?my_filter=20</code> it applies the filter.</p><h3 id="default-parameter-values-and-placeholders" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Default parameter values and placeholders<a class="headerlink" href="#default-parameter-values-and-placeholders" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>Following best practices, you should set default parameter values as follows:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="Default parameter values">Default parameter values</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">%
SELECT * FROM table
WHERE attr &gt; {{Int32(my_filter, 10)}}
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>When you call the endpoint with <code>/v0/pipes/:PIPE.json</code> without setting any value to <code>my_filter</code>, it automatically applies the default value of 10.</p><p>If you don&#x27;t set a default value for a parameter, you should validate that the parameter is defined before using it in the query as explained previously.</p><p>If you don&#x27;t validate the parameter and it&#x27;s not defined, the query might fail. Tinybird populates the parameter with a placeholder value based on the data type. For instance, numerical data types are populated with 0, strings with <code>__no_value__</code>, and date and timestamps with <code>2019-01-01</code> and <code>2019-01-01 00:00:00</code> respectively. You could try yourself with a query like this:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="Get placeholder values">Get placeholder values</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">%
  SELECT 
      {{String(param)}} as placeholder_string,
      {{Int32(param)}} as placeholder_num,
      {{Boolean(param)}} as placeholder_bool,
      {{Float32(param)}} as placeholder_float,
      {{Date(param)}} as placeholder_date,
      {{DateTime(param)}} as placeholder_ts,
      {{Array(param)}} as placeholder_array
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>This returns the following values:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">{
  &quot;placeholder_string&quot;: &quot;__no_value__&quot;,
  &quot;placeholder_num&quot;: 0,
  &quot;placeholder_bool&quot;: 0,
  &quot;placeholder_float&quot;: 0,
  &quot;placeholder_date&quot;: &quot;2019-01-01&quot;,
  &quot;placeholder_ts&quot;: &quot;2019-01-01 00:00:00&quot;,
  &quot;placeholder_array&quot;: [&quot;__no_value__0&quot;,&quot;__no_value__1&quot;]
}
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>When using <code>defined()</code> functions in the <code>WHERE</code> clause, make sure to add <code>1</code> and use the <code>AND</code> operator to avoid SQL syntax errors like:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">SELECT * FROM table
WHERE 1
{% if defined(my_filter) %}
AND attr &gt; {{Int32(my_filter)}}
{% end %}
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h3 id="cascade-parameters" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Cascade parameters<a class="headerlink" href="#cascade-parameters" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>Parameters with the same name in different pipes are cascaded down the dependency chain.</p><p>For example, if you publish pipe A with the parameter <code>foo</code>, and then pipe B which uses pipe A as a data source also with the parameter <code>foo</code>, then when you call the endpoint of pipe B with <code>foo=bar</code>, the value of <code>foo</code> will be <code>bar</code> in both pipes.</p><h2 id="throw-custom-errors" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">Throw custom errors<a class="headerlink" href="#throw-custom-errors" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><p>The following example stops the endpoint processing and returns a 400 error:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="Validate if a param is defined and throw an error if it&#x27;s not defined">Validate if a param is defined and throw an error if it&#x27;s not defined</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">%
{% if not defined(my_filter) %}
{{ error(&#x27;my_filter (int32) query param is required&#x27;) }}
{% end %}
select * from table
where attr &gt; {{Int32(my_filter)}}
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>The <code>custom_error</code> function is an advanced version of <code>error</code> where you can customize the response and other aspects. The function gets an object as the first argument, which is sent as JSON, and the status_code as a second argument, which defaults to 400.</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="Validate if a param is defined and throw an error if it&#x27;s not defined">Validate if a param is defined and throw an error if it&#x27;s not defined</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">%
{% if not defined(my_filter) %}
{{ custom_error({&#x27;error_id&#x27;: 10001, &#x27;error&#x27;: &#x27;my_filter (int32) query param is required&#x27;}) }}
{% end %}
select * from table
where attr &gt; {{Int32(my_filter)}}
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h2 id="errors-and-retries" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">Errors and retries<a class="headerlink" href="#errors-and-retries" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><p>Endpoints return standard HTTP success or error codes. For errors, the response also includes extra information about what went wrong, encoded in the response as JSON.</p><h3 id="error-codes" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Error codes<a class="headerlink" href="#error-codes" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>Endpoints might return the following HTTP error codes:</p><div class="max-w-[calc(100%_+_40px)] overflow-auto -mx-5 ps-5 md:max-w-full md:mx-0 md:ps-0"><table><thead><tr><th>Code</th><th>Description</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>400</td><td>Bad request. A <code>HTTP400</code> can be returned in several scenarios and typically represents a malformed request such as errors in your SQL queries or missing query parameters.</td></tr><tr><td>403</td><td>Forbidden. The auth Token doesn&#x27;t have the correct scopes.</td></tr><tr><td>404</td><td>Not found. This usually occurs when the name of the endpoint is wrong or hasn&#x27;t been published.</td></tr><tr><td>405</td><td>HTTP Method not allowed. Requests to endpoints must use the <code>GET</code> method.</td></tr><tr><td>408</td><td>Request timeout. This occurs when the query takes too long to complete by default this is 10 seconds.</td></tr><tr><td>414</td><td>Request-URI Too Large. Not all APIs have the same limit but it&#x27;s usually 2KB for GET requests. Reduce the URI length or use a POST request to avoid the limit.</td></tr><tr><td>429</td><td>Too many requests. Usually occurs when an endpoint is hitting into rate limits.</td></tr><tr><td>499</td><td>Connection closed. This occurs if the client closes the connection after 1 second, if this is unexpected increase the connection timeout on your end.</td></tr><tr><td>500</td><td>Internal Server Error. Usually an unexpected transient service error.</td></tr></tbody></table></div><p>Errors when running a query are usually reported as 400 Bad request or 500 Internal Server Error, depending on whether the error can be fixed by the caller or not.</p><p>In those cases the API response has an additional HTTP header, <code>X-DB-Exception-Code</code> where you can check the internal database error, reported as a stringified number.</p><h3 id="retries" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Retries<a class="headerlink" href="#retries" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>When implementing an API Gateway, make sure to handle potential errors and implement retry strategies where appropriate.</p><p>Implement automatic retries for the following errors:</p><ul><li>HTTP 429: Too many requests</li><li>HTTP 500: Internal Server Error</li></ul><p>Follow an exponential backoff when retrying requests that produce the previous errors.</p></article><div class="flex items-center justify-end h-10" data-pagefind-ignore="true"><div class="italic text-caption"><span>Updated<!-- --> <time dateTime="2025-10-23T01:34:51.000Z">5 months ago</time></span></div></div><nav class="flex justify-between items-stretch gap-2 md:gap-4 mt-4 border-t border-v-border pt-8" data-pagefind-ignore="true"><div class="flex-1 flex 6l.746.994z"></path></svg></div><div class="flex-1 flex flex-col justify-center p-2 md:p-4 rounded-lg border border-v-border hover:border-v-border-active hover:bg-v-bg-active"><span 94-6ee008eb8be89699.js\",\"9267\",\"static/chunks/9267-89ff5dc708370f39.js\",\"1284\",\"static/chunks/1284-f30446673b9ba073.js\",\"7867\",\"static/chunks/7867-6d0484accd87a171.js\",\"3145\",\"static/chunks/3145-ca0c40eb1bb881d8.js\",\"5107\",\"static/chunks/5107-ef688f2fbbe55825.js\",\"2418\",\"static/chunks/2418-b0d27e6f47546ed6.js\",\"4144\",\"static/chunks/4144-34f98e6e70550e12.js\",\"1147\",\"static/chunks/1147-ac53c80b8f8a3921.js\",\"1749\",\"static/chunks/1749-b2df567f1b8974df.js\",\"5643\",\"static/chunks/5643-5ba78075e5c8bae2.js\",\"1796\",\"static/chunks/1796-b956fe6fe21dbf17.js\",\"787\",\"static/chunks/787-09fc1907ef45c351.js\",\"996\",\"static/chunks/996-ce0ceee74ea8f43a.js\",\"7432\",\"static/chunks/7432-03643de0998568d4.js\",\"1384\",\"static/chunks/app/(forward)/forward/%5B%5B...slug%5D%5D/page-8347ce85311902e7.js\"],\"default\"]\n21:T392c,"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"---\ntitle: Endpoints\nmeta:\n    description: Endpoints make it easy to use the results of your queries in applications.\n---\n\n# {% icon name=\"endpoint\" /%} Endpoints\n\nEndpoints are a type of pipe that you can call from other applications. For example, you can ingest your data, build SQL logic inside a pipe, and then publish the result of your query as a REST API endpoint.\n\n\n\n## Create an endpoint\n\nEndpoints are defined in a .pipe file using the `TYPE ENDPOINT` directive. See [Endpoint pipes](/forward/dev-reference/datafiles/pipe-files#endpoint-pipes).\n\nYou can list your endpoints and their URLs and tokens using the `tb endpoint` command. See [tb endpoint](/forward/dev-reference/commands/tb-endpoint).\n\n## Query parameters\n\nQuery parameters are great for any value of the query that you might want control dynamically from your applications. For example, you can get your endpoint to answer different questions by passing a different value as query parameter.\n\nUse dynamic parameters means to do things like:\n\n- Filtering as part of a `WHERE` clause.\n- Changing the number of results as part of a `LIMIT` clause.\n- Sorting order as part of an `ORDER BY` clause.\n- Selecting specific columns for `ORDER BY` or `GROUP BY` clauses.\n\n### Define dynamic parameters\n\nTo make a query dynamic, start the query with a `%` character. That signals the engine that it needs to parse potential parameters.\n\nAfter you have created a dynamic query, you can define parameters by using the following pattern `{{\u003cdata_type\u003e(\u003cname_of_parameter\u003e[,\u003cdefault_value\u003e, description=\u003c\"This is a description\"\u003e, required=\u003cTrue|False\u003e])}}`. For example:\n\n```sql {% title=\"Simple select clause using dynamic parameters\" %}\n%\nSELECT * FROM TR LIMIT {{Int32(lim, 10, description=\"Limit the number of rows in the response\", required=False)}}\n```\n\nThe previous query returns 10 results by default, or however many are specified on the `lim` parameter when requesting data from that API endpoint.\n\n{% callout type=\"caution\" %}\nBoolean data type does not support the `description` or `required` arguments.\n{% /callout %}\n\n### Call an endpoint with dynamic parameters\n\nWhen using an endpoint that uses parameters, pass in the desired parameters. \n\nUsing the previous example where `lim` sets the amount of maximum rows you want to get, the request would look like this:\n\n```shell {% title=\"Using an endpoint containing dynamic parameters\" %}\ncurl -d https://api.europe-west2.gcp.tinybird.co/v0/pipes/tr_pipe?lim=20\u0026token=\u003cyour_token\u003e\n```\n\n### Available data types for dynamic parameters\n\nYou can use the following data types for dynamic parameters:\n\n- `Boolean`: Accepts `True` and `False` as values, as well as strings like `'TRUE'`, `'FALSE'`, `'true'`, `'false'`, `'1'`, or `'0'`, or the integers `1` and `0`.\n- `String`: For any string values.\n- `DateTime64`, `DateTime` and `Date`: Accepts values like `YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS.MMM`, `YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS` and `YYYYMMDD` respectively.\n- `Float32` and `Float64`: Accepts floating point numbers of either 32 or 64 bit precision.\n- `Int` or `Integer`: Accepts integer numbers of any precision.\n- `Int8`, `Int16`, `Int32`, `Int64`, `Int128`, `Int256` and `UInt8`, `UInt16`, `UInt32`, `UInt64`, `UInt128`, `UInt256`: Accepts signed or unsigned integer numbers of the specified precision.\n\n### Use column parameters\n\nYou can use `column` to pass along column names of a defined type as parameters, like:\n\n```sql {% title=\"Using column dynamic parameters\" %}\n%\nSELECT * FROM TR \nORDER BY {{column(order_by, 'timestamp')}}\nLIMIT {{Int32(lim, 10)}}\n```\n\nAlways define the `column` function's second argument, the one for the default value. The alternative for not defining the argument is to validate that the first argument is defined, but this only has an effect on the execution of the endpoint. A placeholder is used in the development of the pipes.\n\n```sql {% title=\"Validate the column parameter when not defining a default value\" %}\n%\nSELECT * FROM TR\n{\\% if defined(order_by) %}\nORDER BY {{column(order_by)}}\n{\\% end %}\n```\n\n### Pass arrays\n\nYou can pass along a list of values with the `Array` function for parameters, like so:\n\n```sql {% title=\"Passing arrays as dynamic parameters\" %}\n%\nSELECT * FROM TR WHERE \naccess_type IN {{Array(access_numbers, 'Int32', default='101,102,110')}}\n```\n\n### Send stringified JSON as parameter\n\nConsider the following stringified JSON:\n\n```json\n\"filters\": [\n    {\n        \"operand\": \"date\",\n        \"operator\": \"equals\",\n        \"value\": \"2018-01-02\"\n    },\n    {\n        \"operand\": \"high\",\n        \"operator\": \"greater_than\",\n        \"value\": \"100\"\n    },\n    {\n        \"operand\": \"symbol\",\n        \"operator\": \"in_list\",\n        \"value\": \"AAPL,AMZN\"\n    }\n]\n```\n\nYou can use the `JSON()` function to use `filters` as a query parameter. The following example shows to use the `filters` field from the JSON snippet with the stock_prices_1m sample dataset.\n\n```sql\n%\nSELECT symbol, date, high\nFROM stock_prices_1m\nWHERE\n    1\n    {\\% if defined(filters) %}\n        {\\% for item in JSON(filters, '[]') %}\n            {\\% if item.get('operator', '') == 'equals' %}\n                AND {{ column(item.get('operand', '')) }} == {{ item.get('value', '') }}\n            {\\% elif item.get('operator') == 'greater_than' %}\n                AND {{ column(item.get('operand', '')) }} \u003e {{ item.get('value', '') }}\n            {\\% elif item.get('operator') == 'in_list' %}\n                AND {{ column(item.get('operand', '')) }} IN splitByChar(',',{{ item.get('value', '') }})\n            {\\% end %}\n        {\\% end %}\n    {\\% end %}\n```\n\nWhen accessing the fields in a JSON object, use the following syntax:\n\n```\nitem.get('Field', 'Default value to avoid SQL errors').\n```\n\n## Pagination\n\nYou can paginate results by adding `LIMIT` and `OFFSET` clauses to your query. You can parameterize the values of these clauses, allowing you to pass pagination values as query parameters to your endpoint.\n\nUse the `LIMIT` clause to select only the first `n` rows of a query result. Use the `OFFSET` clause to skip `n` rows from the beginning of a query result. Together, you can dynamically chunk the results of a query up into pages.\n\nFor example, the following query introduces two dynamic parameters `page_size` and `page` which lets you control the pagination of a query result using query parameters on the URL of an endpoint.\n\n```sql {% title=\"Paging results using dynamic parameters\" %}\n%\nSELECT * FROM TR\nLIMIT {{Int32(page_size, 100)}}\nOFFSET {{Int32(page, 0) * Int32(page_size, 100)}}\n```\n\nYou can also use pages to perform calculations such as `count()`. The following example counts the total number of pages:\n\n```sql {% title=\"Operation on a paginated endpoint\" %}\n%\nSELECT count() as total_rows, ceil(total_rows/{{Int32(page_size, 100)}}) pages FROM endpoint_to_paginate\n```\n\nThe addition of a `LIMIT` clause to a query also adds the `rows_before_limit_at_least` field to the response metadata. `rows_before_limit_at_least` is the lower bound on the number of rows returned by the query after transformations but before the limit was applied, and can be useful for response handling calculations.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```sql\nSELECT * FROM users WHERE active = true LIMIT 10\n```\n\nResponse might include:\n\n- `rows`: 10 (actual rows returned)\n- `rows_before_limit_at_least`: 1,000 (at least this many active users exist)\n\n**Why \"at least\"?** ClickHouse can stop counting once it knows the answer exceeds the `LIMIT` value. This makes it a lower bound, not an exact count.\n\n**Useful for:**\n\n- Pagination logic (\"showing 10 of at least 1,247 results\")\n- Determining if more results exist without running a separate `COUNT()` query\n\nThis metadata is returned automatically with any `LIMIT` query, saving you from running an additional `COUNT(*)` query to check if more results are available.\n\n{% callout type=\"tip\" %}\nTo get consistent pagination results, add an `ORDER BY` clause to your paginated queries. \n{% /callout %}\n\n## Advanced templating\n\nTo build more complex queries, use flow control operators like `if`, `else` and `elif` in combination with the `defined()` function, which helps you to check if a parameter whether a parameter has been received and act accordingly.\n\nTinybird's templating system is based on the [Tornado Python framework](https://github.com/tornadoweb/tornado), and uses Python syntax. You must enclose control statements in curly brackets with percentages `{%..%}` as in the following example:\n\n```sql {% title=\"Advanced templating using dynamic parameters\" %}\n%\nSELECT\n  toDate(start_datetime) as day,\n  countIf(status_code \u003c 400) requests,\n  countIf(status_code \u003e= 400) errors,\n  avg(duration) avg_duration\nFROM\n  log_events\nWHERE\n  endsWith(user_email, {{String(email, 'gmail.com')}}) AND \n  start_datetime \u003e= {{DateTime(start_date, '2019-09-20 00:00:00')}} AND\n  start_datetime \u003c= {{DateTime(end_date, '2019-10-10 00:00:00')}}\n  {\\% if method != 'All' %} AND method = {{String(method,'POST')}} {\\% end %}\nGROUP BY\n  day\nORDER BY\n  day DESC\n```\n\n### Validate presence of a parameter\n\nTo validate if a parameter is present in the query, use the `defined()` function. For example:\n\n```sql {% title=\"Validate if a param is in the query\" %}\n%\nselect * from table\n{\\% if defined(my_filter) %}\nwhere attr \u003e {{Int32(my_filter)}}\n{\\% end %}\n```\n\nWhen you call the endpoint with `/v0/pipes/:PIPE.json?my_filter=20` it applies the filter.\n\n### Default parameter values and placeholders\n\nFollowing best practices, you should set default parameter values as follows:\n\n```sql {% title=\"Default parameter values\" %}\n%\nSELECT * FROM table\nWHERE attr \u003e {{Int32(my_filter, 10)}}\n```\n\nWhen you call the endpoint with `/v0/pipes/:PIPE.json` without setting any value to `my_filter`, it automatically applies the default value of 10.\n\nIf you don't set a default value for a parameter, you should validate that the parameter is defined before using it in the query as explained previously.\n\nIf you don't validate the parameter and it's not defined, the query might fail. Tinybird populates the parameter with a placeholder value based on the data type. For instance, numerical data types are populated with 0, strings with `__no_value__`, and date and timestamps with `2019-01-01` and `2019-01-01 00:00:00` respectively. You could try yourself with a query like this:\n\n```sql {% title=\"Get placeholder values\" %}\n%\n  SELECT \n      {{String(param)}} as placeholder_string,\n      {{Int32(param)}} as placeholder_num,\n      {{Boolean(param)}} as placeholder_bool,\n      {{Float32(param)}} as placeholder_float,\n      {{Date(param)}} as placeholder_date,\n      {{DateTime(param)}} as placeholder_ts,\n      {{Array(param)}} as placeholder_array\n```\n\nThis returns the following values:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"placeholder_string\": \"__no_value__\",\n  \"placeholder_num\": 0,\n  \"placeholder_bool\": 0,\n  \"placeholder_float\": 0,\n  \"placeholder_date\": \"2019-01-01\",\n  \"placeholder_ts\": \"2019-01-01 00:00:00\",\n  \"placeholder_array\": [\"__no_value__0\",\"__no_value__1\"]\n}\n```\n\nWhen using `defined()` functions in the `WHERE` clause, make sure to add `1` and use the `AND` operator to avoid SQL syntax errors like:\n\n```sql\nSELECT * FROM table\nWHERE 1\n{\\% if defined(my_filter) %}\nAND attr \u003e {{Int32(my_filter)}}\n{\\% end %}\n```\n\n### Cascade parameters\n\nParameters with the same name in different pipes are cascaded down the dependency chain.\n\nFor example, if you publish pipe A with the parameter `foo`, and then pipe B which uses pipe A as a data source also with the parameter `foo`, then when you call the endpoint of pipe B with `foo=bar`, the value of `foo` will be `bar` in both pipes.\n\n## Throw custom errors\n\nThe following example stops the endpoint processing and returns a 400 error:\n\n```sql {% title=\"Validate if a param is defined and throw an error if it's not defined\" %}\n%\n{\\% if not defined(my_filter) %}\n{{ error('my_filter (int32) query param is required') }}\n{\\% end %}\nselect * from table\nwhere attr \u003e {{Int32(my_filter)}}\n```\n\nThe `custom_error` function is an advanced version of `error` where you can customize the response and other aspects. The function gets an object as the first argument, which is sent as JSON, and the status_code as a second argument, which defaults to 400.\n\n```sql {% title=\"Validate if a param is defined and throw an error if it's not defined\" %}\n%\n{\\% if not defined(my_filter) %}\n{{ custom_error({'error_id': 10001, 'error': 'my_filter (int32) query param is required'}) }}\n{\\% end %}\nselect * from table\nwhere attr \u003e {{Int32(my_filter)}}\n```\n\n## Errors and retries\n\nEndpoints return standard HTTP success or error codes. For errors, the response also includes extra information about what went wrong, encoded in the response as JSON.\n\n### Error codes\n\nEndpoints might return the following HTTP error codes:\n\n{% table %}\n  * Code\n  * Description\n  ---\n  * 400\n  * Bad request. A ``HTTP400`` can be returned in several scenarios and typically represents a malformed request such as errors in your SQL queries or missing query parameters.\n  ---\n  * 403\n  * Forbidden. The auth Token doesn't have the correct scopes.\n  ---\n  * 404\n  * Not found. This usually occurs when the name of the endpoint is wrong or hasn't been published.\n  ---\n  * 405\n  * HTTP Method not allowed. Requests to endpoints must use the ``GET`` method.\n  ---\n  * 408\n  * Request timeout. This occurs when the query takes too long to complete by default this is 10 seconds.\n  ---\n  * 414\n  * Request-URI Too Large. Not all APIs have the same limit but it's usually 2KB for GET requests. Reduce the URI length or use a POST request to avoid the limit.\n  ---\n  * 429\n  * Too many requests. Usually occurs when an endpoint is hitting into rate limits.\n  ---\n  * 499\n  * Connection closed. This occurs if the client closes the connection after 1 second, if this is unexpected increase the connection timeout on your end.\n  ---\n  * 500\n  * Internal Server Error. Usually an unexpected transient service error.\n{% /table %}\n\nErrors when running a query are usually reported as 400 Bad request or 500 Internal Server Error, depending on whether the error can be fixed by the caller or not.\n\nIn those cases the API response has an additional HTTP header, `X-DB-Exception-Code` where you can check the internal database error, reported as a stringified number.\n\n### Retries\n\nWhen implementing an API Gateway, make sure to handle potential errors and implement retry strategies where appropriate.\n\nImplement automatic retries for the following errors:\n\n- HTTP 429: Too many requests\n- HTTP 500: Internal Server Error\n\nFollow an exponential backoff when retrying requests that produce the previous errors.\n"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"3c:{\"fill\":\"#25283D\",\"d\":\"M7 4.063a.667.667 0 1 0 0 1.333.667.667 0 0 0 0-1.333m-2 0a.667.667 0 1 0 0 1.333.667.667 0 0 0 0-1.333m4
